Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

Steps to reproduce the problem:



<b class="line"><!---->Steps to reproduce the problem:<!----></b>



<br>





[0] Download linux-release_asan-linux-release-1012365.zip from 



<span class="line"><!---->[0] Download linux-release_asan-linux-release-1012365.zip from <!----></span>





https://www.googleapis.com/download/storage/v1/b/chromium-browser-asan/o/linux-release%2Fasan-linux-release-1012377.zip?generation=1654763766078992&alt=media



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://www.googleapis.com/download/storage/v1/b/chromium-browser-asan/o/linux-release%2Fasan-linux-release-1012377.zip?generation=1654763766078992&amp;alt=media"><!---->https://www.googleapis.com/download/storage/v1/b/chromium-browser-asan/o/linux-release%2Fasan-linux-release-1012377.zip?generation=1654763766078992&amp;alt=media<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





[1] python3 -m http.server 8000



<span class="line"><!---->[1] python3 -m http.server 8000<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[2] Settings→Security→Safe Browsing→enable Enhanced protection



<span class="line"><!---->[2] Settings→Security→Safe Browsing→enable Enhanced protection<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[3] Make sure the folder `/tmp/xxx/CRXTelemetry` is big enough or deep enough that it takes a long time to delete it.(**Note that this is only to increase the race window, you can also add sleep in the InitHelper to omit this step, please apply repro_vuln.diff patch**)



<span class="line"><!---->[3] Make sure the folder `/tmp/xxx/CRXTelemetry` is big enough or deep enough that it takes a long time to delete it.(**Note that this is only to increase the race window, you can also add sleep in the InitHelper to omit this step, please apply repro_vuln.diff patch**)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[3] Run: `/path/to/linux-release_asan-linux-release-1012365/asan-linux-release-1012365/chrome-wrapper --user-data-dir=/tmp/xxx --enable-features=SafeBrowsingExtensionTelemetry,SafeBrowsingExtensionTelemetryPersistence 



<span class="line"><!---->[3] Run: `/path/to/linux-release_asan-linux-release-1012365/asan-linux-release-1012365/chrome-wrapper --user-data-dir=/tmp/xxx --enable-features=SafeBrowsingExtensionTelemetry,SafeBrowsingExtensionTelemetryPersistence <!----></span>





http://127.0.0.1:8000/poc.html`



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="http://127.0.0.1:8000/poc.html`"><!---->http://127.0.0.1:8000/poc.html`<!----></a>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





If all goes well, you should see a browser close the moment it is opened, then trigger the UAF.



<span class="line"><!---->If all goes well, you should see a browser close the moment it is opened, then trigger the UAF.<!----></span>



<br>





You can also adjust the poc to set the SetTimeout



<span class="line"><!---->You can also adjust the poc to set the SetTimeout<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Note that this vulnerability function is not only called when the browser is opened, you can trigger it by enabling Enhanced protection.



<span class="line"><!---->Note that this vulnerability function is not only called when the browser is opened, you can trigger it by enabling Enhanced protection.<!----></span>



<br>





Also similar usages in this file have bugs, please read on for bug reports, they happen in many different places.



<span class="line"><!---->Also similar usages in this file have bugs, please read on for bug reports, they happen in many different places.<!----></span>



<br>





I also triggered another vulnerability and provided ASAN.（ref: asan_write_report.txt)



<span class="line"><!---->I also triggered another vulnerability and provided ASAN.（ref: asan_write_report.txt)<!----></span>



<br>





Here are just the steps to reproduce the vulnerable functions that are easiest to trigger.



<span class="line"><!---->Here are just the steps to reproduce the vulnerable functions that are easiest to trigger.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Problem Description:



<b class="line"><!---->Problem Description:<!----></b>



<br>





[0] ExtensionTelemetryPersister is owned by ExtensionTelemetryService, which derived from KeyedSerive, and will be release after the browser closed.



<span class="line"><!---->[0] ExtensionTelemetryPersister is owned by ExtensionTelemetryService, which derived from KeyedSerive, and will be release after the browser closed.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[1] The InitHelper task with weak_factory_.GetWeakPtr()  is posted to ThreadPool (a separate sequence) in ExtensionTelemetryPersister::PersisterInit，but WeakPtrs are **not** safe to use across multiple threads.



<span class="line"><!---->[1] The InitHelper task with weak_factory_.GetWeakPtr()  is posted to ThreadPool (a separate sequence) in ExtensionTelemetryPersister::PersisterInit，but WeakPtrs are **not** safe to use across multiple threads.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[2] ExtensionTelemetryPersister may be destroyed on the UI thread while InitHelper is running，because InitHelper will perform some file IO operations, such as the recursive deletion of the old_dir directory here(eg: if --user-data-dir=/tmp/xxx, then old_dir is /tmp/xxx/CRXTelemetry).



<span class="line"><!---->[2] ExtensionTelemetryPersister may be destroyed on the UI thread while InitHelper is running，because InitHelper will perform some file IO operations, such as the recursive deletion of the old_dir directory here(eg: if --user-data-dir=/tmp/xxx, then old_dir is /tmp/xxx/CRXTelemetry).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[3] Since ExtensionTelemetryPersister has been released at this time, accessing write_index_ will trigger UAF.



<span class="line"><!---->[3] Since ExtensionTelemetryPersister has been released at this time, accessing write_index_ will trigger UAF.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





```cpp



<span class="line"><!---->```cpp<!----></span>

Additional Comments:



<b class="line"><!---->Additional Comments:<!----></b>



<br>





1. ExtensionTelemetryPersister::ClearPersistedFiles



<span class="line"><!---->1. ExtensionTelemetryPersister::ClearPersistedFiles<!----></span>



<br>





2. ExtensionTelemetryPersister::ReadReport



<span class="line"><!---->2. ExtensionTelemetryPersister::ReadReport<!----></span>



<br>





3. ExtensionTelemetryPersister::WriteReport



<span class="line"><!---->3. ExtensionTelemetryPersister::WriteReport<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





These functions also use the TaskRunner based thread pool , which has similar vulnerabilities and should be fixed as well.



<span class="line"><!---->These functions also use the TaskRunner based thread pool , which has similar vulnerabilities and should be fixed as well.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





An asan log of ExtensionTelemetryPersister::WriteReport is attached here as additional proof. refer to asan_write_report.txt



<span class="line"><!---->An asan log of ExtensionTelemetryPersister::WriteReport is attached here as additional proof. refer to asan_write_report.txt<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





**Since this has multiple paths that could lead to different UAFs, this could be a serious bug, please fix it soon.**



<span class="line"><!---->**Since this has multiple paths that could lead to different UAFs, this could be a serious bug, please fix it soon.**<!----></span>

[1] Interestingly, this module seems to have been fixed once with the race condition UAF, but not completely.



<span class="line"><!---->[1] Interestingly, this module seems to have been fixed once with the race condition UAF, but not completely.<!----></span>

[2] And in this submission on 2022.5.24, the read and write file operations in the thread pool were introduced, which greatly increased the race window and greatly increased the probability of UAF triggering on slow CPUs.

In addition, here I will explain the UAF in ExtensionTelemetryPersister::WriteReport additionally. Since you have fixed a race condition UAF in SaveFile[1], I will not explain more about this race window. I believe it is possible.



<span class="line"><!---->In addition, here I will explain the UAF in ExtensionTelemetryPersister::WriteReport additionally. Since you have fixed a race condition UAF in SaveFile[1], I will not explain more about this race window. I believe it is possible.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Here I explain task_runner_ [0], since task_runner_ is created by ThreadPool::CreateSequencedTaskRunner, task_runner_->PostTask will post a task to the thread pool.



<span class="line"><!---->Here I explain task_runner_ [0], since task_runner_ is created by ThreadPool::CreateSequencedTaskRunner, task_runner_-&gt;PostTask will post a task to the thread pool.<!----></span>



<br>





The possible question here is TaskShutdownBehavior::CONTINUE_ON_SHUTDOWN, according to [this documentation](



<span class="line"><!---->The possible question here is TaskShutdownBehavior::CONTINUE_ON_SHUTDOWN, according to [this documentation](<!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:docs/shutdown.md#step-3-joining-other-threads



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:docs/shutdown.md#step-3-joining-other-threads"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:docs/shutdown.md#step-3-joining-other-threads<!----></a>





)



<span class="line"><!---->)<!----></span>



<br>





-->



<span class="line"><!---->--&gt;<!----></span>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>





ThreadPool shutdown starts. At this point, no new SKIP_ON_SHUTDOWN or CONTINUE_ON_SHUTDOWN task can start running (they are deleted without running). The main thread blocks until all SKIP_ON_SHUTDOWN tasks that started running prior to ThreadPool shutdown start are complete, and all BLOCK_SHUTDOWN tasks are complete (irrespective of whether they were posted before or after ThreadPool shutdown start). When no more SKIP_ON_SHUTDOWN is running and no more BLOCK_SHUTDOWN task is queued or running, the main thread is unblocked and ThreadPool shutdown is considered complete. Note: CONTINUE_ON_SHUTDOWN tasks that started before ThreadPool shutdown may still be running.



<span class="line"><!---->ThreadPool shutdown starts. At this point, no new SKIP_ON_SHUTDOWN or CONTINUE_ON_SHUTDOWN task can start running (they are deleted without running). The main thread blocks until all SKIP_ON_SHUTDOWN tasks that started running prior to ThreadPool shutdown start are complete, and all BLOCK_SHUTDOWN tasks are complete (irrespective of whether they were posted before or after ThreadPool shutdown start). When no more SKIP_ON_SHUTDOWN is running and no more BLOCK_SHUTDOWN task is queued or running, the main thread is unblocked and ThreadPool shutdown is considered complete. Note: CONTINUE_ON_SHUTDOWN tasks that started before ThreadPool shutdown may still be running.<!----></span>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Only the task of SKIP_ON_SHUTDOWN will block the ThreadPool shutdown. If there is only the ExtensionTelemetryPersister::SaveFile CONTINUE_ON_SHUTDOWN task in the thread pool, then even if the ExtensionTelemetryPersister::SaveFile is running, the ThreadPool will shut down, which will not cause the UAF to be triggered.



<span class="line"><!---->Only the task of SKIP_ON_SHUTDOWN will block the ThreadPool shutdown. If there is only the ExtensionTelemetryPersister::SaveFile CONTINUE_ON_SHUTDOWN task in the thread pool, then even if the ExtensionTelemetryPersister::SaveFile is running, the ThreadPool will shut down, which will not cause the UAF to be triggered.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So here I send a large number of SKIP_ON_SHUTDOWN tasks to other thread pool task runner. At this time, the thread pool includes the SKIP_ON_SHUTDOWN task and the ExtensionTelemetryPersister::SaveFile CONTINUE_ON_SHUTDOWN task. At this time, the shutdown of the thread pool is blocked, thus ensuring that the UAF can be triggered.



<span class="line"><!---->So here I send a large number of SKIP_ON_SHUTDOWN tasks to other thread pool task runner. At this time, the thread pool includes the SKIP_ON_SHUTDOWN task and the ExtensionTelemetryPersister::SaveFile CONTINUE_ON_SHUTDOWN task. At this time, the shutdown of the thread pool is blocked, thus ensuring that the UAF can be triggered.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>

<span class="line"><!---->    : profile_(profile), max_num_files_(max_num_files) {<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->  // Shutdown behavior is CONTINUE_ON_SHUTDOWN to ensure tasks<!----></span>

  // are run on the threads they were called on.



<span class="line"><!---->  // are run on the threads they were called on.<!----></span>

  task_runner_ = base::ThreadPool::CreateSequencedTaskRunner( //---->[0]



<span class="line"><!---->  task_runner_ = base::ThreadPool::CreateSequencedTaskRunner( //----&gt;[0]<!----></span>



<br>





      {base::MayBlock(), base::TaskPriority::BEST_EFFORT,

Date: Tue Jun 28 16:56:48 2022



<span class="line"><!---->Date: Tue Jun 28 16:56:48 2022<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Fix Use-After-Free in Persister



<span class="line"><!---->Fix Use-After-Free in Persister<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Fixed the use of weak factory pointers trying to access destroyed



<span class="line"><!---->Fixed the use of weak factory pointers trying to access destroyed<!----></span>



<br>





objects on different threads. The fix involves using SequenceBound



<span class="line"><!---->objects on different threads. The fix involves using SequenceBound<!----></span>



<br>





on the object to ensure that the tasks the object are running and



<span class="line"><!---->on the object to ensure that the tasks the object are running and<!----></span>



<br>





the object itself are running on the same thread.



<span class="line"><!---->the object itself are running on the same thread.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

This CL switched the the persister from using its own task runner, to utilizing sequence bound to ensure that the posted tasks and the persister object are always on the same thread.

Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.

Thanks for the review! We planned to only merging back to 104 as that is the earliest the code would be released. The Extension Telemetry Service has a finch experiment but only beta/dev/canary users are included currently. After the code is merged the GCL file that controls the finch experiment will be updated to ensure that only users with 104+ chrome versions are being served content which will prevent this issue on any 102/103 releases crashing anymore.



<span class="line"><!---->Thanks for the review! We planned to only merging back to 104 as that is the earliest the code would be released. The Extension Telemetry Service has a finch experiment but only beta/dev/canary users are included currently. After the code is merged the GCL file that controls the finch experiment will be updated to ensure that only users with 104+ chrome versions are being served content which will prevent this issue on any 102/103 releases crashing anymore.<!----></span>

objects on different threads. The fix involves using SequenceBound

the object itself are running on the same thread.

Target project:

<label for="targetProjectInput">Target project:</label>


            


              

<input id="targetProjectInput" aria-owns="chops-autocomplete-1" aria-autocomplete="both" aria-expanded="false" aria-haspopup="listbox" aria-activedescendant="">


              




      


        /*
         * Really specific class names are necessary because ShadowDOM
         * is disabled for this component.
         */
        .chops-autocomplete-container {
          position: relative;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container table {
          padding: 0;
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
          color: var(--chops-link-color);
          position: absolute;
          background: var(--chops-white);
          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }
